DEPARTMENT OF BUILDING AND ZONING
WAIVER OF PERMIT FEES
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 14, 2006 from
DONALD H. WLODARSKI, Commissioner, Department of Building and Zoning
respectfully request the granting of a No Fee Permit for the Forest Preserve District of Cook County for
repair of Limestone Shelter S-1 at Allison Woods # 1, 2906 Milwaukee Avenue, Northbrook, Illinois in
Northfield Township.
040680
$ 131.00

Permit #:
Requested Waived Fee Amount:

This request is pursuant to the County Board's adoption of Item No. 176427 on September 16, 1991 that
all building and zoning permit fees be waived for public entities defined as county, township,
municipality, municipal corporation, school district, forest preserve district, park district, fire protection
district, sanitary district, library district and all other local governmental bodies.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $131.00.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the permit fees be waived.
The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE CHIEF JUDGE
ILLINOIS NOT-FOR-PROFIT DISPUTE RESOLUTION ACT
Transmitting a Communication, dated March 28, 2006 from
TIMOTHY C. EV ANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
respectfully request that pursuant to General Administrative Order 2006-01, the Cook County Board of
Commissioners approve the disbursement of funds from the Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Fund,
County Fund 531 (5311452), to the Center for Conflict Resolution (Center). The Center was the only
qualifying applicant for these funds in 2005.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $200,000.00. (531-818 Account).

IN THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS
GENERAL ADMINISTRATIVE ORDER NO. 2006-01
SUBJ ECT: ILLINOIS NOT-FOR-PRO FIT DISPUTE RESOLUTION ACT
Pursuant to the Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act (710, ILCS 2011 et seq.), the Clerk
of the C ircuit Court of Cook County has collected fees from civil filings for the year 2005 for
disbursement to the Dispute Resolution Centers which qualify under said Act and General Order 19 of the
Circuit Court of Cook County. Fees available for disbursement from this Fund for the year 2005 total
$220,495.50.

17

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

Upon review of applications received for funds collected in 2005 the sole qualifying applicant
under the requirements set forth in said Act and General Order No. 19 of the Circuit Court of Cook
County was fo und to be Center for Conflict Resolution. It is eligible for the maximum amount allowable
for disbursement to any Dispute Resolution Center in a given year of $200,000.00.
Pursuant to the Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act (7 10, ILCS 20/1 et seq.), any funds
collected but not disbursed in a given year shall be paid in single county judicial circuits to the County
Treasurer for the ad ministration of justice in the judicial circuit. An amount of $20,495.50 remains
collected for the yea r 2005 but no Dispute Resolution Center is qualified to receive disbursement of these
fund s.
THEREFORE, it is hereby ordered that the amount of $200,000.00, representing the maximum
amount allowable for disbursement to any Dispute Resolution Center in a given year, shall be disbursed
to Center for Conflict Reso lution.
FURTHER, it is hereby ordered that the amoun t of $20,495.50 representing funds collected
under the Illinois Not-For-Profit Dispute Resolution Act for 2003 but not disbursed, shall be disbursed to
the Treasurer of Cook County for the administration of justice in the Circuit Court of Cook County.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the request of the Chief
Judge of the C ircuit Court of Cook County be approved. T he motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE STATE'S ATTORNEY
GRANT AW ARD ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Commun ication, dated March 28 , 2006 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State's Attorney 's Office
requesting authorization to accept a no-cost grant extension from the Department of Justice, Bureau of
Justice Assistance, for the State's Attorneys Juveni le Anti-Weapons Strategy (JAWS) Program, which
will enab le the office to expend the entire grant award. This program seeks to address juvenile gun crime
by targeting the adults who provide weapons for juveniles to use, often in the commission of a crime.
Through the dedication of two (2) investigators and one (I) assistant state's attorney, investigative and
prosecutorial energies will be focused on stemming the flow of weapons into the hands of juveniles who
use them to commit repeat or violent offenses.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on March 6, 2003 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of $992,679.00.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fi scal Impact: None. Supple mental Grant Award: None. Funding period extension: January
1, 2006 through December 31 , 2006.

Administrative Services Bureau of the State's Attorney' s Office be approved . The motion carried
unanimously.

hearing before the Cook County Zoning Board of Appeals on a request for a Special Use, Unique Use on
certain property described therein:
271463

DOCKET #7901 - LAGRANGE HIGHLANDS SANITARY DISTRJCT, Owner, 5900
South Willow Springs Road, LaGrange, Illinois 60525, Application (No. SU-05-05;
205060). Submitted by T-Mobile Wireless, 8550 West Bryn Mawr, Chicago, Illinois
6063 1. Seeking a SPECIAL USE, UN IQUE USE in the R-4 Single Family Residence
District to instal l a wireless communications antenna on an existing water tower and an
equipment shelter/cabinet on the site in Section 17 of Lyons Township. The property
consist of 1.95 acres located on the west side of Willow Springs Road, approximately 250
feet south of Plainfield Road in Lyons Township. Intended use: Insta ll wireless

ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE GRANTING A SPECIAL USE
FOR UNIQUE USE LOCATED IN LYONS TOWNSHIP
AS AUTHORIZED BY THE COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the owner of certai n property located in Lyons Township described in Section l , herein, has
petitioned the Cook County Board of Commissioners for a Special Use for Unique Use pem1it in the R-3
Single Family Residence District; and
WHEREAS, the said petition was received by the Zoning Board of Appeals of Cook County as Docket
#7901 and a public hearing was held in regard to said request after due notice, all in accordance with the
Cook County Zoning Ordinance and the Statutes of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Zoning Board of Appeals entered detailed findings in accordance w ith the standards set
forth in the Ordinance recommending that the Cook County Board of Commissioners grant said
applications for a Special Use for Unique Use permit; and
WHEREAS, it is the determination that said request be granted in accordance with the recommendations
of the Zoning Board of Appeals.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinoi s:
Section 1:

That a Special Use for Unique Use for T-Mobi le Wireless Facility consisting of mounting
antennas on an existing water tower and placing their base station equipment (cabinets)
on a small leased parcel at the base of the water tower be granted.
LEGAL DESCRIPTION
Lots I , 2 and 3 in Ernest D. Conrad 's Willow Springs Road subdivision of the North
3 16.88 ft. of the East 290.40 ft. of the North 112 of the SW 1/4 of Section 17, Township
38 North, Ran ge 12, East of the Third Principal Meridian.

commonly described as approximately 1.95 acres, located on the West side of Willow Springs Rd. ,
approximately 250 ft. South of Plainfield Rd. in Lyons Township.
Section 2:

That the Special Use for Unique Use located in the R-3 Single Family Residence District
as mentioned in Section I of this Ordinance is hereby authorized.

Section 3:

That this Ordinance under the provisions of Section 13.8.9 of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance be in full force and effect from and after its passage and approva l, except that
if said use is not established within one year as provided in Section 13.8.14 said Special
Use for Unique Use shall be null and void. That said property be developed and
constructed pursuant to the detailing set forth in the testimon y and contained in the
exhibits and Findings of the Cook County Zoning Board of Appea ls hereby incorporated
by reference into this Ordinance, as provided by law.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

Chairman Collins inquired whether HMJ Melrose Park, LLC, filed for exempt status prior to closing on
the property.
Jacquelyn Harder, Economic Development Project Director, replied that HMJ Melrose Park, LLC, filed
prior to the date of purchase. This is a common practice; most applicants file for the application for
special circumstances before closing. These applicants want assurance that there will be municipal and
County support.
Chairman Collins stated that the 24 month abandonment issue needs to be examined to determine how the
24 month time span was derived.

No. 276743. The motion carried.

Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS AND BOBBIE L. STEELE
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
RESOLUTION SUPPORTING DISSOLUTION OF SUBURBAN COOK COUNTY
TUBERCULOSIS SANITARIUM DISTRICT
WHEREAS, lllinois Senate Bill 2654, as amended, would dissolve the Suburban Cook County
Tuberculosis Sanitarium District (" TB Di strict"); and
WHEREAS, lllinois Senate Bill 2654, as amended, would transfer the assets and liabilities of the TB
District to the Cook County Board; and
WHEREAS, Illinois Senate Bill 2654, as amended, would require the Cook County Department of
Public Health to assume a ll responsibility for the prevention, care, treatment and control of tuberculosis
wi thin the District; and
WHEREAS, lllinois Senate Bill 2654, as amended, provides that the tax base of the dissolved district
shall be added to the tax base of Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the rllinois Senate has approved Senate Bill 2654, as amended, and the bill is now before
the Illinois House of Representatives for consideration; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners believes that Illinois Senate Bill 2654, as
amended, is in the best interest of the health and welfare of suburban Cook County residents.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby support Senate Bill 2654, as amended, and urges the Illinois House of Representatives to act
during this legislative session to pass this legislation; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that suitable copies of this Resolution be delivered to Governor
Blagojevich, Senate President Emil Jones, Jr., House Speaker Michael J. Madigan, Senator Frank
Watson, Senate Republican Leader, Representative Tom Cross, House Republican Leader and all of Cook
County's duly elected representatives in the General Assembly; and

140

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this Resolution shall take effect on the date of its passage and
approval.

Approved and adopted this 18th day of April 2006.
JOHN H . STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Comm issioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Transmitting a Communication, dated March 28, 2006 from
STEPHEN A. MARTIN, JR., Ph.D. , M.P.H. , Chief Operating Officer, Department of Public Health
requesting approval of the following resolution granting authority to the Chief Operating Officer of the
Cook County Department of Public Health to execute written West Nile Virus Data Sharing and Use
Agreement with participating entities on behalf of the Cook County Board of Commissioners as the
Board of Health of Cook County.
06-R-187
RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners also serves as the Board of Health of Cook
County; and
WHEREAS, the Board has created the Cook County Department of Public Health to carry out the day to
day public health activities in the County; and

143

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

WHEREAS, an essential function under both State law and County ordinance is the detection,
investigation and prevention of infectious, communicable disease; and

WHEREAS, the implementation of surveillance systems to aid local public health departments and their
surveillance partners to efficiently, effectively and detect and monitor, in a timely manner, the occurrence
of an outbreak of disease will affect the public health; and

WHEREAS, the Department ha s a secure web-browser based database and viewer for West Nile Virus
surveillance data known as WNVMAP; and

WHEREAS, WNVMAP will provide a part1c1pating state certified public hea lth department or a
mosquito abatement district access to data analysis which will enable the participant to be aware of a
possible outbreak that may have a serious effect on the public health; and

WHEREAS, the Privacy Rules promulgated pursuant to the Health Insurance Portability and
Accountability Act of 1996 (P.L. 104-191) permit a covered entity to disclose protected health
information, without authorization, to public health authorities who are legally authorized to receive such
information for the purpose of preventing or controlling disease, injury or disability, 45 CFR 
l 64.5 12(b)(1 )(i); and

WHEREAS, participant desires to participate in WNVMAP to better enable it to prepare for and respond
to such an outbreak, which may have a serious effect on the public health of the residents of Cook County
cooperate w ith.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the C hief Operating Officer of the Cook County
Department of Public Health is granted the authority to enter into and execute on behalf of the Board,
West Nile Virus Data Sharing and Use Agreement with participating entities and to terminate such West
Nile Virus Data Sharing and Use Agreement when appropriate.

Approved and adopted this 18th day of April 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR. , President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. T he motion carried unanimously.

THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF FRED SOLARI
WHEREAS, Fred Solari died peacefully at his home in Skokie on March 9, 2006 at the age of 55; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari was the loving husband of Joan, proud father of sons Dan and Andrew and late
son Peter, and a friend of everyone in Chicago' s theater and dance community; and

147

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

WHEREAS, Fred Solari was a fair, warm, determined, honest and gentle man, who, was born in Chicago
and graduated cum laude from the University of Notre Dame and Loyola University Law School; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari was a lawyer by training but followed his Jove for the arts and worked
relentlessly behind the scenes over several decades to revitalize the Athenaeum Theatre on Southport
Avenue in Chicago to create a welcome home for artists while attracting a loyal aud ience, and as a result,
in 1997 was recognized by the Chicago Tribune as one of the 100 most notable contributors to Chicago
arts in the last 150 years; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari arrived at the Athenaeum Theatre in 1970 as a member of the Summer Comedy
Theater, where he and such other young artists as Michael Maggio staged a series of highly successful
performances; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari, along with his wife and sons, transformed the Athenaeum Theater from
something that was similar to a school auditorium into a magnificent theater which now houses a 900-seat
main stage theater, three studio theaters, and a slew of offices, along with a beautiful marquee, an
e levator, remodeled dressing rooms, a new orchestra pit and improved lighting; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari was the invaluable Executive Director of the Athenaeum Theatre for the last 11
years and during that time co-founded the theater' s groundbreaking Dance Chicago festiva l, which
celebrated sma ll troupes every November, and under his leadership the Athenaeum Theater became a
galvanizing force, contributing to local dance and fostering countless artists in dance, theater and music;
and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari's leadership allowed thousands of Cook County residents to enj oy quality
perfonnances and helped make Cook County the strongest regional theater area in the United States; and
WHEREAS, during his career, Fred Solari also worked at the Apollo Theatre, the Shubert Theatre, the
Woodstock Opera House, C ivic Opera House and served as Chief Executive Officer of Civic Stages of
Chicago where he helped to present the annual Spring Festival of Dance, which was a major downtown
event, and collaborated with other producers on several local and international arts events in the 1980s
and early 1990s; and
WHEREAS, Fred Solari will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friend s of Fred Solari
and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Fred
Solari so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 18th day of Apri l 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,

ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF FRANK B. FOSTER
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster died in Evanston on April 3, 2006 at the age of90; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster, born on February 25, 1916 in Evanston and preceded in death by his loving
wife, Phoebe, was the devoted father of two sons, Frank B. Foster, Jr. and Timothy Foster, loving brother
of his sister Edith Hicks, and proud grandfather of two grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster will long be remembered as a successful businessman with a great wit who
contributed generously to the suburban Cook County community and enjoyed among other things,
reading, gardening, needlepoint, swimming, classical music and Shakespeare; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster was a 1937 graduate of Lafayette College in Easton, Pennsylvania and was
drafted into the United States Army Quartermaster Corps in 1941 and rose to the rank of major; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster returned to Evanston in 1946 and began working at Quinlan and Tyson,
Inc., as an associate and later went on to become its president during which ti me he played a major role in
making the company one of the largest and most successful property management firms in the area by the
1960s; he retired from Quinlan and Tyson in 198 1; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster was active in a number of charitable causes including making a major
contribution to the Evanston Community Foundation to help establish its own offices when it separated
from the United Way in 1999; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster's civic involvement also included the Evanston Rotary Club, where he
served as past president and was the oldest living Rotarian in Evanston having been admitted to the
Rotary Club of Evanston in May 1920, the same year that club was chartered; and

149

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster was a former member of the Evanston Plan Commission and the Evanston
Township High School District Board of Education; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster was given various awards and recognitions for his tremendous c1v1c
involvement including the special Community Leade rship Award from the Evanston Chamber of
Commerce; and
WHEREAS, Frank B. Foster was a past president, volunteer and significant benefactor of the Historical
Society where there is the Frank B. Foster Research Room and the Presbyterian Homes where he was a
resident, volunteer and where there is the Frank B. Foster Pavilion.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friend s of Frank B.
Foster and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Frank
B. Foster so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 18th day of April 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR. , President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. T he motion carried unanimously.

EXECUTIVE SESSION
Transmitting a Communication, dated April 11 , 2006 from
JOHNNY C. BROWN , Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook County
respectfully requesting that the minutes of the March 28, 2006 meeting of the Joint Conference
Committee of Stroger Hospital of Cook County be placed on the agenda for the April 18, 2006 meeting of
the Board of Commissioners to be considered in Executive Session. The request for a closed session is
made pursuant to the Open Meetings Acts, 5 ILCS 120/2(c)(I 7): " the recruitment, credentialing,
discipline or forma l peer review of physicians or other health care profess ionals for a hospital, or other
institution providing medical care, that is operating by the public body." Moreover, this matter is
confidentia l pursuant to the Illinois Medical Studies Act, 735 ILCS 5/8-210 I through 5/8-2105 .

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

150

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR APRIL 18, 2006

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Regular Session be recessed
and that the Executive Session be convened for the purpose of considering the minutes of the March 28,
2006 meeting of the Joint Conference Committee of Stroger Hospital of Cook County pursuant to the
Open Meetings Act 5 lLCS I 20/2(c)( 17): " the recruitment, credentialing, discipline or formal peer review
of physicians or other health care professionals for a hospital, or other institution providing medical care,
that is operating by the public body." T he motion carried and the Board of Commissioners convened

in Executive Session.
BOARD RECONVENED
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Executive Session be
adjourned and that the Regular Session be reconvened. The motion carried and the Board of

Commissioners reconvened Regular Session.
Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Board adopt the
recommendation contained in the minutes of the Executive Session of March 2 8, 2006 meeting of the
Joint Conference Committee of the Medical Staff of Stroger Hospital of Cook County, which
recommendation is documented in the back up material attached to the April 17, 2006 letter from Dr.
Daniel Winship to the Board of Commissioners. The motion carried.

Commissioner Maldonado voted "no".
Commissioner Sims voted "present".

ADJOURNMENT
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved that the meeting do now adjourn to
meet again at the same time and same place on Wednesday, May 3, 2006, in accordance with County
Board Resolution 06-R-09.
The motion prevailed and the meeting stood adjourned.
